  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

Popular Answered Questions

<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/298741-what-did-you-think-of-the-movie-adaptation">What did you think of the movie adaptation of Nick &amp; Norah&#39;s Infinite Playlist ?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_298741'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F25373.Nick_Norah_s_Infinite_Playlist">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/298741-what-did-you-think-of-the-movie-adaptation">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/298741-what-did-you-think-of-the-movie-adaptation">See all 8 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/43373150-kalli"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1561746125i/43373150._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/43373150-kalli">Kalli</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It's probably hard for me to answer this question just because this book has come to define such a large part of my life. I really didn't like the mov<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It's probably hard for me to answer this question just because this book has come to define such a large part of my life. I really didn't like the movie. I felt that it just wasn't the right medium for the message that was being told, which wasn't really about music, or partying, or even having an end goal but about the fact that life is scary, unpredictable, and will throw you curve balls but that it's up to you to surround yourself with people who you can trust to get you through it. <br /><br />The entire plot of the movie was changed for the sake of it being...well a movie. As it is a movie there had to be a specific goal in mind: find Caroline, versus the book which is very much about taking a risk, and setting out into this scary, mystery that is life with no plan in the hopes that everything will work out. However, the fact that Norah spends most of the movie searching for Caroline really compromises Nick and Norah's relationship. In the book Norah and Nick are discovering each other on purpose, Norah runs away and then she comes back, or Nick retreats into himself before snapping out of it. The story and narrative is driven by their intentional discovery of each other and themselves no by a the need to resolve a plot. In the movie this is lost because it seems that the characters are forced together more so by circumstance than by choice. In this way there is no active effort being made on their part to get over their respective exes and move-on, it's more of just a side effect of being stuck in the same van searching for Caroline. This really affects their characters. For example, Nick comes off a lot more mopey; in the book his sadness over Tris is also edged with bitterness, versus in the movie it is defined by blue-lit, ethereal scenes that make him out to be a lost, nerdy boy who will never get past Tris. <br /><br />Another thing that made me really sad about the movie is the way it approaches the relationships between Tris, Caroline, and Norah. I come from an all-girls school background and the relationships between these three girls really reminded me of that when I read the book (i.e. it was authentic.) In fact when I forced one of my closest friends to read the book one of his first comments was that the female relationships in the book really reminded him of the way I describe my own relationships with girls at my schools. This is because even though Norah and Caroline don't necessarily like Tris they are still quite familiar, i.e. they're close enough that Norah has listened to Nick's mixtapes, and some of Tris' flirting tricks were taught to her by Norah (the back of the car phone call). Further, Tris is never outright mean to Norah in the book, passive aggressive sure, but they clearly have a past and the issue is less about how she treats Norah and more about how she has treated Nick. In the movie they are all reduced to caricatures. Norah becomes the outcast, Tris becomes the popular mean girl who has picked on the outcast, and Caroline becomes the drunk, dumb one. They're relationship is squashed in the interest in telling an underdog story; (Norah is clearly not suppose to be an underdog by the way, she is rich, smart, and attractive, her problems are not defined by society but by her own ability to shut down her emotions, and push people away). <br /><br />Finally the movie focuses way too much on keeping in small, meaningful symbols as opposed to actually meaningful moments (maybe this was a budget thing). Meaningful, material symbols I can think of include Salvatore's jacket, and the Yugo, and meaningful moments that were left out or butchered include moments such as the 'I Wanna Hold Your Hand' Monologue. I capitalize it because this was one of the most important parts of the book. It is important because it is said by Dev, a notorious 'man-whore' for lack of a better term who truly believes in the idea that love is simple, and not sexual, almost more-so like a friendship than anything, which contrasts the stereotypical image of his character. In the movie this is spoken by Thom, and that ruins it. Throughout the story Thom and his boyfriend are already exhibiting a healthy relationship and this has not had an impact on Nick through out his break up with Tris. Nick has become a cynic, and turns to people like Dev as evidence as to why maybe its best not to risk it all on one person like he did with Tris. This is why it is so significant when Dev tells him that love is not only possible but simple. This entire night Nick has been over analyzing his relationship with Norah and here is Dev explaining that his own non-monogamous behavior is not evidence that love cannot happen but evidence that when you have a feeling you need to follow it or love will NEVER happen. This is what allows Nick to take a chance on Norah, and move past Tris.<br /><br />Let's be real, the book is written in beautiful prose that does not transpose well into a movie script. Too much of the story is meant to be self-reflective, and internal and that is difficult to do when you can't show a character's thought process, or inner-monologue. The movie is probably a great indie flick if you haven't read the book, but if you've read the book and had it resonate with you the way I have than it will be a disappointment. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/630544-can-anyone-help-me-figure-out-norah-s">Can anyone help me figure out Norah&#39;s relationship with Caroline? I couldn&#39;t understand why she was so cherished by Norah&#39;s parents. Was it one of the &quot;my parents want me to be someone else&quot; type of thing?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_630544'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F25373.Nick_Norah_s_Infinite_Playlist">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/43373150-kalli"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1561746125i/43373150._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/43373150-kalli">Kalli</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think it was a lot of that, but also driven a lot by the fact that Norah and Caroline have grown up together. The vibe I got was that Caroline kind <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think it was a lot of that, but also driven a lot by the fact that Norah and Caroline have grown up together. The vibe I got was that Caroline kind of felt like another daughter to them, and that because Norah cared about her so much her parents had long ago come to cherish Caroline in the same way. I think this mainly because there does not seem to be a lot of resentment from Norah towards Caroline, it's more like "oh my gosh my parents are ridiculous and love my best friend so much that it's kind of crazy". <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

<div id="review_97951674" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97951674" />
    <a title="unknown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2863914-unknown"><img alt="unknown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579703867p2/2863914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97951674?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="unknown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="unknown" href="/user/show/2863914-unknown">unknown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780756979492" href="/book/show/6279543-nick-and-norah-s-infinite-playlist">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">me, age 14</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to unknown by: </span>
      the movie
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=52-in-2010">52-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=seen-on-film">seen-on-film</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=30-day-book-challenge">30-day-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2863914-unknown?shelf=vote-getters">vote-getters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97951674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13588363078622228608">A few years ago I posted a far-too-personal blog on MySpace (ok, so maybe it was more than a few years ago) offering a retrospective analysis of select mortifying excepts from my circa-age 14 journal (note: not a diary). It's the only year I kept one, and thank god, because while it's perhaps worthwhile to have a snapshot of what I was thinking and feeling at that particular, tumultuous time in my life, what I was thinking and feeling was <i>stupid</i> and the way I went about putting it into words was</span>
  <span id="freeText13588363078622228608" style="display:none">A few years ago I posted a far-too-personal blog on MySpace (ok, so maybe it was more than a few years ago) offering a retrospective analysis of select mortifying excepts from my circa-age 14 journal (note: not a diary). It's the only year I kept one, and thank god, because while it's perhaps worthwhile to have a snapshot of what I was thinking and feeling at that particular, tumultuous time in my life, what I was thinking and feeling was <i>stupid</i> and the way I went about putting it into words was <i>even worse</i> and no one should ever have to revisit their emotional idiocy in such stark and concrete fashion. Ever. As a rule, teenagers are not good at analyzing the world, or their feelings, or their feelings about the world. Because they are idiots.<br /><br />Take, for example, the lead characters of Nick and Norah's Infinite Playlist: they are idiots. This account of their madcap adventures, both sonic and sexual, across a very busy night in Manhattan during their senior year of high school is a lot of fun to read, but it's also excruciating, because it is written so accurately in the alternating dear-diary voices of a teenage boy and a teenage girl, respectively, and wow, you probably don't really want to be quite so inside a 17-year-old's mind, even one as seemingly jaded and witty as Norah, the cynical rich daughter of a recording industry exec who meets cute with tragically sensitive emo punk &amp; damaged romantic Nick. Because all of her oh-so-learned insights about the world, which probably would have seemed really wise-beyond-her-years if she was real and I knew her when I was 17 myself and totally in love with her even though I would never actually say anything to her about my feelings? Self-centered, self-indulgent claptrap. <br /><br />And don't get me started on Nick: his chapters are even worse. Whether he's moping about his big breakup or waxing poetic about his new attraction to Norah, he sounds like nothing so much as if he is stringing together crappy lyrics from bad emo songs (<i>"I open my mouth and she opens my mouth and it's like she's breathing right through me. And her body is wet and it's right against mine and I want, I want, I want."</i>). There's this section where he goes on and on about how beautiful and wonderful it is to just stand out in the rain, to really <i>be</i> in the rain, you know? And this part is just so painful for me to read because my very own <s>diary</s> journal has a long section about how I was feeling confused and conflicted about this girl so I just went out at night and went rollerblading in the rain and it was just so <i>quiet</i> and <i>true</i> and man do I want to punch 14-year-old me in the face (though it did subsequently spark the creation of my own bad emo song parody, Rollerblading in the Rain, which goes like this: <i>"Needing you/ wishing you/ hoping you/ wanting you/ is like rollerblading in the rain/ you might slip and fall but you'll/ pick yourself up again</i>").<br /><br />So what exactly does it mean that N&amp;NIP is written so accurately in the voices of its characters that it is regularly frustratingly twee and trite, because hey, what are the musings of teenagers if not twee and trite? It's like the Showgirls conundrum: is that a really really bad movie about a stripper, or is it a really really smart, intentionally bad genre parody? Either way, both entertainments are actually <i>entertaining</i>, even if I remain unconvinced of their genius, so I guess that's something.<br /><br />A side note about Nick &amp; Norah: The Movie - I like it. I think it benefits from a more focused structure and a wider cast of characters to take the pressure off the occasionally insufferable leads. Plus it has a great soundtrack. On the other hand, the book doesn't have Michael Cera's terrifying face. Who expected he would grow up to so closely resemble The Penguin?<br /><br /><i>Facebook 30 Day Book Challenge Day 13: Book whose main character is most like you.</i> (Most like me as a teenager anyway.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13588363078622228608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_25871198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25871198" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/314550-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565913182p2/314550.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25871198?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/314550-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375835339" href="/book/show/944704.Nick_Norah_s_Infinite_Playlist">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">pretentious punk rocker wannabes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Anna by: </span>
      I have no one to blame -- I foolishly picked it up myself in the
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/314550-anna?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/314550-anna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/314550-anna?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25871198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11546365786015388778">This book left such a bad taste in my mouth! Where do I begin...?<br/><br/>First, the language was <i>ridiculous</i>. This is supposed to be a young adult book, yet I can't tell you how many times the authors [over]used the word "fuck." Why? In most of the situations it was <i>totally</i> unnecessary and sounded like they were trying too hard to impress their young readers. I understand that "fuck" is a word just like anything else, but just like every other word in the English language, it does not need to be the <i>only</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11546365786015388778" style="display:none">This book left such a bad taste in my mouth! Where do I begin...?<br /><br />First, the language was <i>ridiculous</i>. This is supposed to be a young adult book, yet I can't tell you how many times the authors [over]used the word "fuck." Why? In most of the situations it was <i>totally</i> unnecessary and sounded like they were trying too hard to impress their young readers. I understand that "fuck" is a word just like anything else, but just like every other word in the English language, it does not need to be the <i>only</i> verb or adjective ever used to describe anything! <br /><br />Secondly, I was really disappointed by the way these authors portrayed Norah, the female protagonist. She was a really weak female character. Her self-esteem seemed to depend entirely on how the men in her life felt about her. Whether it was ex-bf Tal or Nick or even her dad, Norah cared more about what the males thought of her than how she actually saw herself. A sad fact and a sad message to be sending young girls who read this book.<br /><br />Also, I did not like the fact that the girls called each other "bitch." Again, this is blatant overuse of a swear word for the purpose of creating shock value. This way of talking, where you use misogynistic terms so easily, is disrespectful and gets at girls' self-esteem, whether or not she realizes it. Civil people don't use the word "bitch" and "fuck" every five minutes. I promise. I am an adult. I use it when I need to but not every other word out of my mouth is "fuck this" and "bitch that." It's not cool and it saddens me that this book is sending the message that it is. <br /><br />In general, I was pretty disappointed by this book. I think it glorified all the wrong things and sent the message that being "cool" is all about what kind of music you listen to and who you know, not the kind of person you actually are. I was terribly annoyed with the seemingly endless pretentious-sounding references to pop culture, punk rock, and the Manhattan lifestyle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11546365786015388778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_39069164" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39069164" />
    <a title="Keith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1290678-keith"><img alt="Keith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1214963010p2/1290678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39069164?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Keith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Keith" href="/user/show/1290678-keith">Keith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39069164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4269850824819509124">My wife loved this book and dragged me to the movie shortly after it came out. I thought the movie was cute---a better than average teen romance set in my old stomping grounds of New York City's Greenwich Village and Soho. On leaving the theater, I soon heard from my wife how much better the book was, and how disappointing the movie was. I guess it's all a question of what you're expecting going in...<br/><br/>I started reading the book as soon as we got home.<br/><br/>It opens with a great hook. Nick sees his ex-g</span>
  <span id="freeText4269850824819509124" style="display:none">My wife loved this book and dragged me to the movie shortly after it came out. I thought the movie was cute---a better than average teen romance set in my old stomping grounds of New York City's Greenwich Village and Soho. On leaving the theater, I soon heard from my wife how much better the book was, and how disappointing the movie was. I guess it's all a question of what you're expecting going in...<br /><br />I started reading the book as soon as we got home.<br /><br />It opens with a great hook. Nick sees his ex-girlfriend at a club and doesn't want to face her. So he turns to the girl next to him, Norah, and asks her to be his girlfriend for five minutes. Surprisingly, she responds by kissing him. Over the course of an all-night adventure in New York, they get to know each other better while each wrestles with their own doubts and insecurities and tries to figure out what to think of the other.<br /><br />I loved it! And my wife was right about the movie.<br /><br />The lead characters were likable and realistic. Their concerns and doubts, their hopes and fears, the roller coaster of she loves me, she loves me not, all resonated with the distant memories of my teen years. The fact that the story is set in a realistic New York City was a bonus. The story wasn't always predicable (despite having seen the movie!) and included a nicely humorous touch to keep things from getting too serious (or too overwhelmed with teen angst).<br /><br />In reading through other reviews, here and on other sites, I'm surprised by the number of people who find the casual cursing and implied sexuality objectionable. I don't know quite how to respond. It's <i>realistic</i> fiction. And these things are part of reality, especially for teenagers on the cusp of adulthood. Obviously younger kids are probably not ready for, and wouldn't understand, some aspects of the real world. But I think this book would be fine for most high school kids. I doubt they will find much here (except perhaps the night life of New York) that they haven't heard about, thought about, and talked about with their peers. In fact, the biggest surprise for a high school reader may be the authors' empathy for the doubts and fears and ups and downs of teen life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4269850824819509124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2057865983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2057865983" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2057865983?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2057865983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11707469260365022414">I have yet to read a David Levithan book that doesn’t move me. I ADORE his writing style. I also ADORE his mind. The way he thinks, the way his characters think. It’s very curious. They often do the unexpected.<br/><br/>Honestly, this wouldn’t have worked if it had been written by somebody else. The faking-you-have-a-girlfriend thing is so overdone I would have cried of exasperation if it had been what this book was all about.<br/><br/>Luckily it’s not. By the way, Rachel Cohn does a good job of writing Norah’s cha</span>
  <span id="freeText11707469260365022414" style="display:none">I have yet to read a David Levithan book that doesn’t move me. I ADORE his writing style. I also ADORE his mind. The way he thinks, the way his characters think. It’s very curious. They often do the unexpected.<br /><br />Honestly, this wouldn’t have worked if it had been written by somebody else. The faking-you-have-a-girlfriend thing is so overdone I would have cried of exasperation if it had been what this book was all about.<br /><br />Luckily it’s not. By the way, Rachel Cohn does a good job of writing Norah’s chapters also. This duo of writers works. Back to the cliché, fortunately it only lasts for a second. Nick and Norah meet because of ex-girlfriend Tris, but they connect because of who they are as a person and who they are together.<br /><br />This is a one-day-one-night type of book. The time frame is a day. Everything that occurs in this book starts the moment the two main characters meet and ends when the night ends. I guess this is why it’s so short. But it’s also why it’s so engrossing. <br /><br />So much is happening and so many thoughts wander in the characters’ minds. They need to figure out a lot of things. Nick has to finally get over Tris and Norah has someone to get out of her mind too. Can they help each other move on? Though it’s about real connection, not simply ‘‘rebounding.’’ <br /><br />Very realistic. Did not get many of the music references so that was a bummer, but the story itself rocks. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11707469260365022414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5278916563086216776">*DISCLAIMER: I wrote this review several years ago...I've grown since then and I realize this review is very BASHING. I really try hard not to write bashing reviews now because there's an author on the other end of a book. Still, I don't want to censor this review because it was what I felt at the <i>time</i> I read it and I still agree with the majority of the sentiments. I wanted to let you know I would approach my review an entirely different way if I had written it now. 7/13<br/><br/>Nick sees his old girlfr</span>
  <span id="freeText5278916563086216776" style="display:none">*DISCLAIMER: I wrote this review several years ago...I've grown since then and I realize this review is very BASHING. I really try hard not to write bashing reviews now because there's an author on the other end of a book. Still, I don't want to censor this review because it was what I felt at the <i>time</i> I read it and I still agree with the majority of the sentiments. I wanted to let you know I would approach my review an entirely different way if I had written it now. 7/13<br /><br />Nick sees his old girlfriend coming towards him with a new guy and he can't let her see him like this, so he asks the girl next to him to be his girlfriend for just five minutes.<br /><br />This book was trash - complete and total trash, with the F-word making an appearance at least every other page and other profanities littered across the story I found it highly offensive and vulgar. I didn't have to read much to realize what kind of book this would become, and needless to say, I did not finish this book. I cannot respect authors who degrade the name of literature by peppering their novels with filth and immorality. I was not impressed with the writing style, nor the characters and felt that having each chapter switching characters was tedious and annoying because they always backtracked. Now you are probably wondering why I even picked up this book in the first place, good question! I had seen it several places and it's name and cover art had been logged in my mind and I decided to put it on hold. The story line is totally unrealistic, and has these two unhappy people who become boy-friend and girl-friend for five minutes to both avoid people and find that they might just have found someone who Really understand them...yeah, right. I was disgusted with their methods of kissing random strangers so they could keep their "pride" in front of people who weren't even worth caring about. I find it really annoying how the people in the book can take one look at someone else and know their character and personality traits, all with just one discerning glance, you expect me to believe that the girl can look at the boy and know exactly what he is like and what he needs? Puh-lease. With novels like this gracing our bookstore shelves it's no wonder teenagers act the way they do. When they read books like this with no morals and a "feels good so do it" attitude how can you expect them to make good choices?<br /><br />*Taken from my book reviews blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2008/05/book-review-79-nick-and-norahs-infinite.html">http://reviewsatmse.blogspot.com/2008...</a></span>

  <span id="freeText3682812830413246764" style="display:none">This book is FUCKING EPIC. <div id="review_22007116" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22007116" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22007116?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375835339" href="/book/show/944704.Nick_Norah_s_Infinite_Playlist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=read-personally-by-moi">read-personally-by-moi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22007116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5588591398625437976">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Before I start the story that is Nick and Norah, I decided we needed to get some misconceptions out of the way first. <br/><br/>1) I don't live in Manhattan, so I won't understand what the characters are talking about. Wrong! I don't live in Manhattan--actually, I've never been farther East than Ohio, but I still got the gist of the story quite easily. Sure, I might never have visited Times Square, but I've been on the Square in my hometown (population 3,400), and the sa</span>
  <span id="freeText5588591398625437976" style="display:none">Reviewed by Me for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Before I start the story that is Nick and Norah, I decided we needed to get some misconceptions out of the way first. <br /><br />1) I don't live in Manhattan, so I won't understand what the characters are talking about. Wrong! I don't live in Manhattan--actually, I've never been farther East than Ohio, but I still got the gist of the story quite easily. Sure, I might never have visited Times Square, but I've been on the Square in my hometown (population 3,400), and the same types of things went on there that go on in New York. <br /><br />2) This book is full of cursing. Right! And if you haven't heard a lot of curse words (do I really need to spell them out?), especially from the mouths of teens, in the last twenty years or so, I'm guessing you live on a commune somewhere in the middle of Utah. <br /><br />3) This book only covers one night. Right again! And oh, what a night it is! One night, filled with all the ups, downs, and sideways that being a teen in todays world brings. <br /><br />Now that we've got that out of the way, we can concentrate on the story. It's about Nick, a bassist for a band with an ever-changing name, who recently had his heart broken by a b***h named Tris. It's about Norah, an uber-complicated girl with more issues than The National Enquirer, who not too long ago had her virginity broken by Tal. And then there's Caroline, and Jessie, and Uncle Lou, not to mention Dev and Thom, and Randy from Are You Randy?, and Hunter from Hunter. There's beer, and there's drugs, and there's sex, although none of it is Nick or Norah's. <br /><br />There's heartbreak, and devastation, and lust, and forgiveness, and acceptance. There's parents to deal with, and friends to attempt to deal with, and a boy and a girl who wish that, just once, they could be themselves and not deal at all. There's a love story, and a song about a girl on a street in the middle of the night, and a band that just might make it big, and a car that won't start, and a subway ride that requires jumping the turnstyle. <br /><br />There's love, and anger, and disappointment, and desperation, and redemption. There's life, and then there's Nick and Norah. There's a story here, and you need to read it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5588591398625437976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1745888310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1745888310" />
    <a title="John Winston" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16673620-john-winston"><img alt="John Winston" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467070596p2/16673620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1745888310?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Winston" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Winston" href="/user/show/16673620-john-winston">John Winston</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1745888310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18424807215330557619">This is probably the worst book I’ve read to date, and I wouldn’t post this review if I thought it would have a negative impact on the authors’ careers. But it won’t so here goes. There’s absolutely no character development here, none. The love story never really gets started (or I probably had something else in mind for a story). <br/><br/>We stay in Norah’s mind soooo much it feels claustrophobic, and trust me, that’s not a mind you want to be in for too long. The F bomb is dropped on almost every page </span>
  <span id="freeText18424807215330557619" style="display:none">This is probably the worst book I’ve read to date, and I wouldn’t post this review if I thought it would have a negative impact on the authors’ careers. But it won’t so here goes. There’s absolutely no character development here, none. The love story never really gets started (or I probably had something else in mind for a story). <br /><br />We stay in Norah’s mind soooo much it feels claustrophobic, and trust me, that’s not a mind you want to be in for too long. The F bomb is dropped on almost every page by every character, which would be OK if it was realistic, but it’s not. The run on sentences by author, Rachel Cohn in particular make an irritating read even more annoying. There’s no reason for them. They don’t add anything. Author intrusion by Cohn is also stark, evidenced by an unrealistic playlist, constant political and religious jabs (not teenager-like), and this pre-occupation with sexual diversity. I’m all for multiculturalism and diversity, but it should play out naturally, not be rammed down our literary throats. <br /><br />Speaking of multiculturalism, where are the brothers and sisters, the people of color, any kind of color? Just sayin’. I only finished this book for two reasons; it was short at less than 200 pages, and it was part of a book club, so I saw it as my literary duty. Ugh! Two stars are pushing it on this. On a good note, David Levithan’s good writing shines through, and the two stars are his and his alone. I like his character, Nick, and his chapters, but half a book does not a whole book make. And the movie was just as bad. There’s enough great stories out there. Who options this stuff? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18424807215330557619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_62998201" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62998201" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62998201?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375835339" href="/book/show/944704.Nick_Norah_s_Infinite_Playlist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=blog">blog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62998201" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18415013776512881450">Nick and Norah meet in a punk rock club one night when Nick asks Norah to be his 5 minute girlfriend. Why? Because Nick's ex, Tris, is in the club with her new man and Tris broke Nick's heart. From that point on, Nick and Norah recognize the chemistry between them, but their feelings are compromised by their previous relationships.<br/><br/>The book is okay. Just okay. Told in stream-of-consciousness chapters alternating between Nick's point of view and Norah's, some of it becomes repetitive (although thi</span>
  <span id="freeText18415013776512881450" style="display:none">Nick and Norah meet in a punk rock club one night when Nick asks Norah to be his 5 minute girlfriend. Why? Because Nick's ex, Tris, is in the club with her new man and Tris broke Nick's heart. From that point on, Nick and Norah recognize the chemistry between them, but their feelings are compromised by their previous relationships.<br /><br />The book is okay. Just okay. Told in stream-of-consciousness chapters alternating between Nick's point of view and Norah's, some of it becomes repetitive (although this technique does allow the reader to see how each experienced and interpreted various situations differently). <br /><br />My main complaint: Nick and Norah are cool. Obnoxiously cool. They are so much smarter and edgier than everyone else and, here's the thing with characters like that, there are people who are genuinely edgy and cool and original--and then there are those who are trying too hard to be so. Nick and Norah fall into the "trying too hard" category. They make obscure cultural references (many of which seem to be more in keeping with the time period of the authors' teenage years and not so much today's teens; for instance, maybe the movie <i>Heathers</i> and the television show <i>My So Called Life</i> are still a big deal to today's teenage crowd, but I somehow doubt it), they have both have a single-minded devotion to on-the-fringe punk bands, and engage in endless fashion critiques regarding what a person's dress reveals about character. They're trying so hard I wonder if and when they'll ever have any fun in life.<br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://viiamanda.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Insignificant Cinder</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18415013776512881450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_17851018" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17851018" />
    <a title="N" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/121445-n"><img alt="N" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529142264p2/121445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17851018?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="N" class="user" itemprop="url" name="N" href="/user/show/121445-n">N</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/121445-n?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/121445-n?shelf=teen">teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17851018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8309950362094158790">On the emo (punk? oh whatever, EMO) music scene in New York City, Nick and Norah meet and fall in love over a single, remarkable night. Unfortunately, what had the potential to be a great book fails in its execution.<br/><br/>The trouble with a co-written book (Cohn and Levithan wrote alternating chapters, sending the manuscript back and forth) is that half the writing I liked a lot (Cohn's) and half the writing I damn near hated (Levithan's). I like wordplay. I do not, however, like it nearly as much as </span>
  <span id="freeText8309950362094158790" style="display:none">On the emo (punk? oh whatever, EMO) music scene in New York City, Nick and Norah meet and fall in love over a single, remarkable night. Unfortunately, what had the potential to be a great book fails in its execution.<br /><br />The trouble with a co-written book (Cohn and Levithan wrote alternating chapters, sending the manuscript back and forth) is that half the writing I liked a lot (Cohn's) and half the writing I damn near hated (Levithan's). I like wordplay. I do not, however, like it nearly as much as Levithan. After about ten pages of his incessant wordplay, I wanted to stab myself in the face. Also, for such a slender novel (even for a teen novel), there was a hell of a lot of <i>ramble</i>. I suspect this is a result of the unplanned, back-and-forth way the novel was written. (There's also a bit near the end where the fourth wall is all but demolished: Levithan screws up the continuity on who exactly Dev's boytoy is; Cohn uses Norah as a mouthpiece to ream him about it during the next chapter.) Perhaps inevitably, after the first few chapters, the story descends into "and then this happened, and then this, and then, and then, and then". I like novels to have a tight story arc. This novel was a sprawling mess.<br /><br />Billed as a love story, it's really not. There's about 30% falling-in-love stuff. The rest is angst about ex-boyfriends and -girlfriends. Realistic? Sure. Fun to read? No. There are chapters and chapters where Nick and Norah do nothing except obsess over their exes. It would be more forgivable if what love stuff there was didn't veer into rather cloying, romance novel territory.<br /><br />The thing to love about this novel is how well the authors inhabit a generation. So much of it rings true. The authors evoke the current youth culture impressively well. (I sound so old. "Young culture". Whatever. It's not my generation. And for the record, an eighteen-year-old would not mourn the cancellation of MSCL. She would have been SEVEN when it was airing. Jeez.) These are the kids I recognize from shows and I'm pretty thrilled to read a book that does them justice. I suppose my beef with the novel is that it tries so hard to be original, but fails. It's only a stale story rebranded for a new generation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8309950362094158790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7684620" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7684620" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75857-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556514715p2/75857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7684620?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/75857-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7684620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10626084462495122581">Novels written by two authors can go one of two ways: they can be really cool, or really bad. Happily, writers of young adult novels seem to have a knack for working in collaboration. "Nick and Norah's Infinite Playlist" (from 2006) was written by Rachel Cohn and David Levithan. Cohn wrote Norah's part and Levithan wrote Nick's part, but they are not really Nick and Norah.<br/><br/>The story starts in the middle of the night (or is it the beginning of the morning?) at a club on Ludlow Street in New York C</span>
  <span id="freeText10626084462495122581" style="display:none">Novels written by two authors can go one of two ways: they can be really cool, or really bad. Happily, writers of young adult novels seem to have a knack for working in collaboration. "Nick and Norah's Infinite Playlist" (from 2006) was written by Rachel Cohn and David Levithan. Cohn wrote Norah's part and Levithan wrote Nick's part, but they are not really Nick and Norah.<br /><br />The story starts in the middle of the night (or is it the beginning of the morning?) at a club on Ludlow Street in New York City. Nick is "the nonqueer bassist in a queercore band who is filling the room with undertone" as his band tears through their set. His life is seeming pretty great when Tris, The Ex, walks into the club. That's where Norah comes in.<br /><br />Norah is "the daughter of an Englewood Cliffs-livin', fat-cat record company CEO" who happens to be in the right place at the exact time that Nick really needs a five-minute girlfriend. That also happens to be right when Norah needs to get a ride for her friend.<br /><br />So it all kind of works out. It also sets the stage for the novel: a first date that makes it through the club scene in New York, a date where everything goes wrong (or maybe it goes right), a date that goes on and on--in a good way, mostly.<br /><br />In other words, "Nick and Norah's Infinite Playlist" is a fast story. Events jump around and the prose moves just as quickly. Cohn and Levithan keep up this speed with their narratives (Nick and Norah get alternating chapters) which have the verve appropriate to a hip, teen novel.<br /><br />Because this book really is firmly grounded in the Young Adult genre. Older readers who have an interest in music (or the upcoming movie) might be interested but the novel is very centered on teen concerns and interests. None of which is a bad thing since this is a YA novel.<br /><br />The narrative here is really tight. Cohn and Levithan do a great job keeping the story coherent as they alternate chapters without getting redundant. I really like the style here. The duel narratives overlap enough that readers get to see key events from Nick and Norah's point of view. This technique helps to give a fuller version of the story as well as humorously showing how differently two people can see the exact same thing.<br /><br />My only qualm with the novel is the language. There is a lot of cursing. That doesn't bother me ideologically, but it does start to seem over the top. About two thirds into the novel I started to wonder if anyone could really curse that much in day-to-day conversation (Norah is a self-proclaimed "potty mouth" to be fair), but maybe I just hung out with a different kind of set when I was younger.<br /><br />"Nick and Norah's Playlist" is a crazy ride of a novel. It has music, borscht, romance, and some great dialogue. Readers familiar with Levithan's other novels ("Boy Meets Boy" to name one) will recognize his frank writing style here. I haven't read any of Cohn's other novels ("Gingerbread" to name one) but she's definitely on my watch list now.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my blog <a href="http://www.missprint.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Print</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10626084462495122581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16833886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16833886" />
    <a title="Morgan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/955972-morgan"><img alt="Morgan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602714071p2/955972.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16833886?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan" href="/user/show/955972-morgan">Morgan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Morgan by: </span>
      Dawn Foster
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/955972-morgan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/955972-morgan?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/955972-morgan?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16833886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5678356198244661543">I noticed this book in our house--my mom was reading it, and the cover both intrigued me and repelled me. However, after my mom's recommendation, I read this book--and loved it. It is one of the most dead-on accurate books I've ever read about young emotions and feelings. The initial plot is slightly contrived: a heartbroken teenager sees his ex with her new guy and asks a girl to pretend she's his girlfriend. However, the story is told by both Nick and Norah's point of view, so the reader is al</span>
  <span id="freeText5678356198244661543" style="display:none">I noticed this book in our house--my mom was reading it, and the cover both intrigued me and repelled me. However, after my mom's recommendation, I read this book--and loved it. It is one of the most dead-on accurate books I've ever read about young emotions and feelings. The initial plot is slightly contrived: a heartbroken teenager sees his ex with her new guy and asks a girl to pretend she's his girlfriend. However, the story is told by both Nick and Norah's point of view, so the reader is allowed into the minds of both characters, allowing for deeper insights into these young people. Rachel Cohn and David Levithan co-wrote this book, and as I said, completely nailed the angst, heartbreak, humor, tragedy, and hope that young love brings. This book is also extremely honest: characters are gay, doped up, drunk, sexual, and misguided. But the honesty and genuine emotion separate this book from the thousands of other young-adult novels from which to choose. A must-read for anyone currently in or who survived their teenage years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5678356198244661543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_384785591" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384785591" />
    <a title="Anthony Chavez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876333-anthony-chavez"><img alt="Anthony Chavez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314570438p2/4876333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384785591?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Chavez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Chavez" href="/user/show/4876333-anthony-chavez">Anthony Chavez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781615579891" href="/book/show/7628741-nick-and-norah-s-infinite-playlist">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384785591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13597998776780122307">I envision Nick working somewhere like The Strand which was featured in "<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7741325.Dash___Lily_s_Book_of_Dares' title='Dash & Lily's Book of Dares by Rachel Cohn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dash & Lily's Book of Dares</a>" and now I understand some of the places that were mentioned in that book and the bathroom writing on the wall they mentioned in "<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7741325.Dash___Lily_s_Book_of_Dares' title='Dash & Lily's Book of Dares by Rachel Cohn' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dash & Lily's Book of Dares</a>" by the same authors.<br/><br/>After reading it I was trying to think of what the writing reminded me of, what with all the musical references and the language used, and I went back to my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9807119.Textual_Healing' title='Textual Healing by Eric Smith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Textual Healing</a> review and thought, "YES." It's like a feel goo</span>
  <span id="freeText13597998776780122307" style="display:none">I envision Nick working somewhere like The Strand which was featured in "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7741325.Dash___Lily_s_Book_of_Dares" title="Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares by Rachel Cohn" rel="nofollow noopener">Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares</a>" and now I understand some of the places that were mentioned in that book and the bathroom writing on the wall they mentioned in "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7741325.Dash___Lily_s_Book_of_Dares" title="Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares by Rachel Cohn" rel="nofollow noopener">Dash &amp; Lily's Book of Dares</a>" by the same authors.<br /><br />After reading it I was trying to think of what the writing reminded me of, what with all the musical references and the language used, and I went back to my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9807119.Textual_Healing" title="Textual Healing by Eric Smith" rel="nofollow noopener">Textual Healing</a> review and thought, "YES." It's like a feel good teen romantic comedy, loaded with musical and pop culture references. I imagined the soundtrack that would be playing to the background of it as I was reading it and would often flip to the beginning of the book to see the map and "The Acknowledgements Playlist," I really dug that those were included. <br /><br />Many reviews of the book harp on the use of the F word. I don't know, maybe I have become desensitized to the word but either I didn't notice it and it didn't matter or it just flowed with the book and I skimmed right past it without another thought. It fit. It worked. Let's move on past the small details. <br /><br />There is nothing special about the storyline, that's not what grabs the reader in my opinion. It's a typical boy-meets-girl/girl-meets-boy type of story but its the execution of the story that seals the deal. The switching of points of view and way it is written while at the same time not taking itself too seriously. I like the non-cliche and non-sappy poetic lines thrown by both Nick and Norah on their alternating chapters, and the lyrics Nick throws together throughout the evening. It drives the point home that every sentence in the book is well thought out. <br /><br />I wasn't entirely taken with the ending. I mean, after everything you've been through that night, going into an ice room with him, and getting into a car with him, and a train, and an elevator and eating and dancing and so on - all those leaps of faith you took with a person who WAS a complete stranger, you are now going to try and decide whether to jump over a turnstile and actually make that into a metaphor about your relationship with him? AND after already making a BIG decision and ditching him once in a taxi. I don't know - it was a little cheesy I thought, but it works. I think it would have been nice if at the end he takes her home, kisses her good night/good morning, she closes the door, runs to her room and looks out the window to try to get one last glimpse of him to remember this night and their meet cute. But hey, that's just me.<br /><br />In my opinion this story is a wild adventure AND all taking place in the span of one night which makes it even wilder. A lot of teenagers and even adults can relate to it though, it touches sensitive areas from intimacy, getting over an ex, making plans for the future, etc. And as I have said before it is one for music lovers as well. It was a fun light read, and a good escape for a week. It was also a good follow up to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2914097.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a>, another good young adult/teen read. Recommended for the romantic teen comedy types out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13597998776780122307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1810181551" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1810181551" />
    <a title="Joanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17348951-joanna"><img alt="Joanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475418532p2/17348951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1810181551?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanna " href="/user/show/17348951-joanna">Joanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1810181551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7262604120468329105">Hello Book Peeps <br/><br/>When I saw the cover for this book and the movie poster when it came out in theatres, I believed that this was going to be some kind of rom com that was sweet, inspirational and maybe even deep. Instead what I found out, in about half a minute into the 1st chapter of this audiobook, was that I was not going to find any of the above mention in this book. What I was going to get was an answer to Axel Rose's infamous question: "Do you know where you are?" Yes Axel, I do. I'm in the</span>
  <span id="freeText7262604120468329105" style="display:none">Hello Book Peeps <br /><br />When I saw the cover for this book and the movie poster when it came out in theatres, I believed that this was going to be some kind of rom com that was sweet, inspirational and maybe even deep. Instead what I found out, in about half a minute into the 1st chapter of this audiobook, was that I was not going to find any of the above mention in this book. What I was going to get was an answer to Axel Rose's infamous question: "Do you know where you are?" Yes Axel, I do. I'm in the jungle baby.<br /><br />Welcome to the Jungle and pretty much every track off the Appetite For Destruction album is the perfect soundtrack for this book about Nick and Nora's very first and very long date. Its hard to believe that this book took place all in the span of one evening. I mean we have all had that night out with friends that started with a plan and quickly took a turn which lead to a series of unfortunate events accompanied by a playlist.<br /><br />Nick and Nora are made for each other. They are super pretentious and judge-y for sure but they are also pretty hilarious too. I did find myself laughing at a lot of the shenanigans they got up to through out the book but they were not characters that I would ever want to re read again.<br /><br />This is a really niche specific type book and I feel that if you are not even remotely comfortable in that niche then your just going to think these two are douches. Who knows, maybe this is the type of story that can only be told as a movie. I guess I will find out when I finally get around to watching it. In the meantime...<br /><br />Happy Reading <br /><br />Jo</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13007968320701297499"><blockquote>
  <b>We are graced, and we are together, and the twoliness is trumping the loneliness and the doubt and the fear.</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I actually liked this a lot. I had a minor issue with it, but other than that it was a fun and short read. I've come to expect great things from David Levithan and Rachel Cohn. Their characters are always so real and believable, and the struggles we read about are things most of us have actually been through and therefore can totally relate to.<br/><br/><b>The worst:</b><br/>♫ The language in this is way to</span>
  <span id="freeText13007968320701297499" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>We are graced, and we are together, and the twoliness is trumping the loneliness and the doubt and the fear.</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />I actually liked this a lot. I had a minor issue with it, but other than that it was a fun and short read. I've come to expect great things from David Levithan and Rachel Cohn. Their characters are always so real and believable, and the struggles we read about are things most of us have actually been through and therefore can totally relate to.<br /><br /><b>The worst:</b><br />♫ The language in this is way too overdone with swearing.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>I mean, they're only the best punk band out there right now, named for the fucking apathy of a xenophobic fucking nation oblivious to the fucking terror it's leaders wreak on the rest of the world (...)</b>
</blockquote><br />Seriously? I would take the essence of this thought much more seriously if there wasn't unnecessary swearing in it. Who talks like this?<br /><br /><br /><b>The best:</b><br />♫ <b>Finally</b>, there's a book with the right idea.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>Maybe the simple diagnosis of either hetero or homo is misleading. Maybe there's just sexuality, and it's bendable and unpredictable, like a circus performer (...)</b>
</blockquote><br />Wouldn't our lives be so much simpler if we didn't have to worry about labels? If we could just <b>be</b> and not be thin or fat or homossexual or...?<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>

<div id="review_1901641419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1901641419" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1901641419?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375890765" href="/book/show/6998754-nick-norah-s-infinite-playlist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=tbr-2017">tbr-2017</a>,
